HISTOGRAMS
==========
  Each histogram is given as 1000 pairs of values (i.e. two columns side by side).
  In each case the left column is the value of the parameter or term (i.e. x value)
  and the right column is the estimated posterior probability (i.e. y value).
  HPD (Highest Posterior Density) intervals are estimated, and may be incorrect: 
  Possible HPD footnotes: 
       '?' HPD interval may be incorrect due to multiple peaks
       '#' HPD may not be useful - posterior density does not reach low levels near either the upper or the lower limit of the prior

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------
     curve height is an estimate of the posterior probability
      each term is the product of a population parameter (e.g. q0) and a migration rate (e.g.m0>1) 
      migration rates are in the coalescent (backwards in times), so that a population migration rate of 
        q1m0>1  is the population rate (forward in time) at which population 1 receives migrants from population 0
